<p>Until recently, bicycle manufacturing was a major industry: the city was the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Raleigh_(bicycle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Raleigh (bicycle)">Raleigh Cycles</a> in 1886, later joined by <a href="/wiki/Sturmey-Archer" title="Sturmey-Archer">Sturmey-Archer</a>, the developer of three-speed hub gears. However, Raleigh's factory on Triumph Road, famous as the location for the filming of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_and_Sunday_Morning_(film)" title="Saturday Night and Sunday Morning (film)">Saturday Night and Sunday Morning</a></i>, was demolished in 2003 to make way for the University of Nottingham's expansion of its <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_Campus" class="mw-redirect" title="Jubilee Campus">Jubilee Campus</a>. The schools and aerial photographers, H Tempest Ltd, were Nottingham-based for many years, until relocating to St. Ives (<a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>) around 1960.
</p><p>Nottingham is also host to the UK's first and only local authority-owned and not-for-profit energy company: <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_Energy" title="Robin Hood Energy">Robin Hood Energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Nottingham was ranked in the top 10 UK cities for job growth (from 2004 to 2013), in the public and private sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> And in the same year, it was revealed that more new companies were started in Nottingham in 2014-15 than in any other UK city, with a 68% year-on-year increase.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Council_house_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Council_house_1.JPG/170px-Council_house_1.JPG" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Council_house_1.JPG/255px-Council_house_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Council_house_1.JPG/340px-Council_house_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Council_house_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Exchange Arcade inside the Council House</div></div></div>
<p>In 2014, Nottingham came seventh in CACI's Retail Footprint rankings of retail expenditure in the UK, behind the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End of London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">I make that 6th</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This is a slip of four places since 2010, primarily due to major developments in other parts of the UK and a relative lack of investment in Nottingham. However <a href="/wiki/Intu_Properties" title="Intu Properties">Intu</a>, the owners of the two main shopping centres (the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Centre" title="Victoria Centre">Victoria Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Broadmarsh_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadmarsh Centre">Broadmarsh Centre</a>) have plans to upgrade and extend them both.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Victoria Centre was built on the site of the former <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Victoria_railway_station" title="Nottingham Victoria railway station">Nottingham Victoria railway station</a>, and was the first to be built in the city, with parking for up to 2,400 cars on several levels, and a bus station.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Nottingham City Council, then owners of the Broadmarsh Centre, had been trying to redevelop it for "almost two decades".<sup id="cite_ref-BBCNEWS_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNEWS-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Work on redeveloping Broadmarsh, at a cost of £400<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million (creating 400 stores, 136,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> of shopping space), was due to start in 2008.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> However, the economic downturn meant that redevelopment was delayed throughout from 2008 to 2010. In the light of the Victoria Centre's redevelopment plans, Westfield announced in 2011 that it was once again planning a £500<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million development of Broadmarsh, which would start in 2012. This, however, did not happen either. Broadmarsh was finally sold to Capital Shopping Centres, the owners of the Victoria Centre. The purchase prompted an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Competition_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Competition Commission (United Kingdom)">Competition Commission</a>, who were concerned that the company's monopoly over the city's shopping centres could have a negative impact on competition.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> CSC subsequently rebranded itself and the centres use the "Intu" name. Although the new owners wished to start the planned development of the Victoria Centre, Nottingham City Council insisted that Broadmarsh must have priority, with the Council offering £50<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million towards its redevelopment.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The deputy leader of Nottingham City Council said the Council would withhold planning permission for the development of the Victoria Centre until they saw "bulldozers going into the Broadmarsh Centre."<sup id="cite_ref-BBCNEWS_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNEWS-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_shopping_outlets">Other shopping outlets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other shopping outlets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Smaller shopping centres in the city are <a href="/wiki/The_Exchange_Arcade" class="mw-redirect" title="The Exchange Arcade">The Exchange Arcade</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Flying_Horse_Walk" title="Flying Horse Walk">Flying Horse Walk</a> and newer developments in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinity_Square_(Nottingham)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trinity Square (Nottingham) (page does not exist)">Trinity Square</a> and The Pod. The <a href="/wiki/Bridlesmith_Gate" title="Bridlesmith Gate">Bridlesmith Gate</a> area has numerous designer shops, and is the home of the original <a href="/wiki/Paul_Smith_(fashion_designer)" title="Paul Smith (fashion designer)">Paul Smith</a> boutique. There are various side streets and alleys with some interesting and often overlooked buildings and shops—such as Poultry Walk, West End Arcade and Hurts Yard. These are home to many specialist shops, as is Derby Road, near the Roman Catholic Cathedral and once the antiques area.
</p><p>Nottingham has a number of <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department stores</a> including the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Fraser" title="House of Fraser">House of Fraser</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_Partnership" title="John Lewis Partnership">John Lewis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enterprise_zone">Enterprise zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Enterprise zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2011, the government announced the creation of <b>Nottingham Enterprise Zone</b>, an <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Enterprise zone">enterprise zone</a> sited on part of the <a href="/wiki/The_Boots_Estate" class="mw-redirect" title="The Boots Estate">Boots Estate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In March 2012, Nottingham Science Park, Beeston Business Park and Nottingham Medipark were added to the zone.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In December 2014, the government announced that the zone would be expanded again, to include Infinity Park Derby, a planned business park for aerospace, rail and automotive technology adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Holdings" title="Rolls-Royce Holdings">Rolls-Royce</a> site in <a href="/wiki/Sinfin" title="Sinfin">Sinfin</a>, Derby.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative-quarter">Creative-quarter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Creative-quarter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Creative Quarter is a project started by Nottingham City Council as part of the Nottingham City Deal. Centred on the east of the city (including the Lace Market, Hockley, Broadmarsh East, the Island site and BioCity), the project aims at creating growth and jobs. In July 2012, the government contributed £25<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million towards a £45<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> fund, mainly targeted at the Creative Quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sky_Mirror,_Nottingham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sky_Mirror%2C_Nottingham.jpg/220px-Sky_Mirror%2C_Nottingham.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sky_Mirror%2C_Nottingham.jpg/330px-Sky_Mirror%2C_Nottingham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sky_Mirror%2C_Nottingham.jpg/440px-Sky_Mirror%2C_Nottingham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sky_Mirror,_Nottingham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Nottingham Playhouse and the Roman Catholic Cathedral reflected in <a href="/wiki/Anish_Kapoor" title="Anish Kapoor">Anish Kapoor</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sky_Mirror" title="Sky Mirror">Sky Mirror</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nottingham has two large-capacity theatres, the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Playhouse" title="Nottingham Playhouse">Nottingham Playhouse</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Nottingham" title="Theatre Royal, Nottingham">Theatre Royal</a>, which together with the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Nottingham Royal Concert Hall">Royal Concert Hall</a> forms the Royal Centre. The city also contains smaller theatre venues such as the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Arts_Theatre" title="Nottingham Arts Theatre">Nottingham Arts Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lace_Market_Theatre" title="Lace Market Theatre">Lace Market Theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Theatre_(Nottingham)" class="mw-redirect" title="New Theatre (Nottingham)">New Theatre</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Galleries_and_museums">Galleries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Galleries and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city contains several notable museums and art galleries including:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_National_Justice_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The National Justice Museum (page does not exist)">The National Justice Museum </a> – Museum of Law Trust based at the Shire Hall in the <a href="/wiki/Lace_Market" title="Lace Market">Lace Market</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Green%27s_Windmill" class="mw-redirect" title="Green&#39;s Windmill">Green's Windmill</a> and Science Centre – A unique working windmill in the heart of the city that was home to the 19th-century mathematical physicist and miller, <a href="/wiki/George_Green_(mathematician)" title="George Green (mathematician)">George Green</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Castle_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham Castle Museum">Nottingham Castle Museum</a> – home to the city's fine and decorative art collections, along with the Story of Nottingham galleries, and the Sherwood Foresters Regimental Museum.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Contemporary" title="Nottingham Contemporary">Nottingham Contemporary</a> – Contemporary art gallery, which opened in 2009.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Art_Exchange" title="New Art Exchange">New Art Exchange</a> - Contemporary art gallery, the largest in the UK dedicated to showing diverse artists, opened in 2008</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Industrial_Museum" title="Nottingham Industrial Museum">Nottingham Industrial Museum</a> – in <a href="/wiki/Wollaton_Park" title="Wollaton Park">Wollaton Park</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Natural_History_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham Natural History Museum">Nottingham Natural History Museum</a> – based at <a href="/wiki/Wollaton_Hall" title="Wollaton Hall">Wollaton Hall</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Videogame_Arcade" class="mw-redirect" title="National Videogame Arcade">National Videogame Arcade</a> – Museum showing recognition, history and the games of the past to the present, based in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Creative_Quarter&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Creative Quarter (page does not exist)">Creative Quarter</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinemas">Cinemas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cinemas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is a <a href="/wiki/Cineworld" title="Cineworld">Cineworld</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Showcase_Cinemas" title="Showcase Cinemas">Showcase</a> in the city. Independent cinemas include the <a href="/wiki/Arthouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthouse">Arthouse</a> <a href="/wiki/Broadway_Cinema" title="Broadway Cinema">Broadway Cinema</a> in Hockley,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and the four-screen <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> <a href="/wiki/Savoy_Cinema,_Nottingham" title="Savoy Cinema, Nottingham">Savoy Cinema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_entertainment">Music and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Music and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Hall,_Nottingham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Albert_Hall%2C_Nottingham.jpg/170px-Albert_Hall%2C_Nottingham.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Albert_Hall%2C_Nottingham.jpg/255px-Albert_Hall%2C_Nottingham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Albert_Hall%2C_Nottingham.jpg/340px-Albert_Hall%2C_Nottingham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Hall,_Nottingham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Albert_Hall,_Nottingham" title="Albert Hall, Nottingham">Albert Hall, Nottingham</a>, one of the city's music venues</div></div></div>
<p>Nottingham has several large music and entertainment venues including the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Nottingham Royal Concert Hall">Royal Concert Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_City_(club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock City (club)">Rock City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Nottingham Royal Concert Hall">Nottingham Royal Concert Hall</a> (2,500-capacity) and the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham Arena">Nottingham Arena</a> (Social centre). Nottingham's <a href="/wiki/City_Ground" title="City Ground">City Ground</a> played host to rock band <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a> in 2005, the first time a concert had been staged at the football stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham also has a selection of smaller venues, including the <a href="/wiki/Albert_Hall,_Nottingham" title="Albert Hall, Nottingham">Albert Hall</a> (800-capacity), <a href="/wiki/Ye_Olde_Salutation_Inn" title="Ye Olde Salutation Inn">Ye Olde Salutation Inn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malt_Cross" title="Malt Cross">Malt Cross</a>, Rescue Rooms, the Bodega, the Old Angel, the Central, the Maze, the Chameleon and the Corner. 1960s Blues-rock band <a href="/wiki/Ten_Years_After" title="Ten Years After">Ten Years After</a> formed in Nottingham, as did the 1970s pop act <a href="/wiki/Paper_Lace" title="Paper Lace">Paper Lace</a> and the critically acclaimed <a href="/wiki/Tindersticks" title="Tindersticks">Tindersticks</a>. Since the beginning of the 2010s, the city has produced a number of artists to gain media attention, including; <a href="/wiki/Jake_Bugg" title="Jake Bugg">Jake Bugg</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Grammar" title="London Grammar">London Grammar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana_(singer)" title="Indiana (singer)">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sleaford_Mods" title="Sleaford Mods">Sleaford Mods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Duncan" title="Natalie Duncan">Natalie Duncan</a>, Ady Suleiman, <a href="/wiki/Dog_Is_Dead" title="Dog Is Dead">Dog Is Dead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Raymond_(musician)" title="Saint Raymond (musician)">Saint Raymond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Childhood_(band)" title="Childhood (band)">Childhood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rue_Royale,_Band" class="mw-redirect" title="Rue Royale, Band">Rue Royale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spotlight_Kid_(band)" title="Spotlight Kid (band)">Spotlight Kid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amber_Run" title="Amber Run">Amber Run</a>.
</p><p>Nottingham is home to <a href="/wiki/Earache_Records" title="Earache Records">Earache Records</a>, a large independent record label setup in Nottingham in 1986 and famously home to <a href="/wiki/Napalm_Death" title="Napalm Death">Napalm Death</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carcass_(band)" title="Carcass (band)">Carcass (band)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entombed_(band)" title="Entombed (band)">Entombed (band)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rival_Sons" title="Rival Sons">Rival Sons</a> and more.
</p><p>The city has an active <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a> scene, with long-established ensembles such as the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Nottingham Symphony Orchestra">city's Symphony Orchestra</a>, Philharmonic Orchestra, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Harmonic_Society" title="Nottingham Harmonic Society">Nottingham Harmonic Society</a>, Bach Choir, Early Music Group Musica Donum Dei and the Symphonic Wind Orchestra giving regular performances in the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sumac_Centre" title="Sumac Centre">Sumac Centre</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Social_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Social centre">social centre</a> in Forest Fields.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wollaton_Park" title="Wollaton Park">Wollaton Park</a> in Nottingham hosts an annual family-friendly music event called <a href="/wiki/Splendour_in_Nottingham" title="Splendour in Nottingham">Splendour</a>. In 2009 it was headlined by <a href="/wiki/Madness_(band)" title="Madness (band)">Madness</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Pogues" title="The Pogues">the Pogues</a>. The following year it was headlined by <a href="/wiki/The_Pet_Shop_Boys" class="mw-redirect" title="The Pet Shop Boys">the Pet Shop Boys</a> and featured, among others, <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noisettes" title="Noisettes">Noisettes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athlete_(band)" title="Athlete (band)">Athlete</a> and <a href="/wiki/OK_Go" title="OK Go">OK Go</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, it featured headline acts <a href="/wiki/Scissor_Sisters" title="Scissor Sisters">Scissor Sisters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blondie_(band)" title="Blondie (band)">Blondie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eliza_Doolittle_(singer)" title="Eliza Doolittle (singer)">Eliza Doolittle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feeder_(band)" title="Feeder (band)">Feeder</a>. In 2012, performers included <a href="/wiki/Dizzee_Rascal" title="Dizzee Rascal">Dizzee Rascal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Razorlight" title="Razorlight">Razorlight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_B" title="Katy B">Katy B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hard-Fi" title="Hard-Fi">Hard-Fi</a>. In 2014, Wollaton Park hosted the first-ever No Tomorrow Festival, featuring the likes of <a href="/wiki/Sam_Smith_(singer)" title="Sam Smith (singer)">Sam Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Grammar" title="London Grammar">London Grammar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clean_Bandit" title="Clean Bandit">Clean Bandit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham is known for its <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> scene.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Rofl Audio Recording Studios opened in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_crafts">Arts and crafts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Arts and crafts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Hockley Arts Market runs alongside <a href="/wiki/Sneinton" title="Sneinton">Sneinton</a> Market.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are several hundred restaurants in Nottingham, with there being several <a href="/wiki/AA_rosette" class="mw-redirect" title="AA rosette">AA rosette</a> winning restaurants in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Iberico World Tapas, located in the city centre, was awarded a Bib Gourmand in the 2013 Michelin Guide.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
Sat Bains, on the edge of the city, near Clifton Bridge, is a two-star Michelin restaurant.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG/170px-Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG/255px-Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG/340px-Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham_Market_Square_Ferris_Wheel.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel" title="Ferris wheel">Ferris wheel</a> in Old Market Square</div></div></div>
<p>In 2010, the city was named as one of the "Top 10 Cities to Visit in 2010" by <a href="/wiki/DK_Publishing" class="mw-redirect" title="DK Publishing">DK Travel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 it was estimated the city received 247,000 overseas visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a Robin Hood Pageant in Nottingham in October. The city is home to the Nottingham Robin Hood Society, founded in 1972 by Jim Lees and Steve and Ewa Theresa West.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2008, a <a href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel" title="Ferris wheel">Ferris wheel</a> was put up in the Old Market Square and was an attraction of Nottingham City Council's "Light Night" on 8 February. The wheel returned to Nottingham in February 2009 to mark another night of lights, activities, illuminations and entertainment. Initially marketed as the Nottingham Eye, it was later redubbed as the Nottingham Wheel, to avoid any association with the <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> It was seen again in 2010 and 2015.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottinghamstreet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Nottinghamstreet.jpg/220px-Nottinghamstreet.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Nottinghamstreet.jpg/330px-Nottinghamstreet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Nottinghamstreet.jpg/440px-Nottinghamstreet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottinghamstreet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New buildings on the south side of the <a href="/wiki/Lace_Market" title="Lace Market">Lace Market</a> area</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many local businesses and organisations use the worldwide fame of Robin Hood to represent or promote their brands. Many residents converse in the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_English" title="East Midlands English">East Midlands dialect</a>. The friendly term of greeting "Ay-up me duck" is a humorous example of the local dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> but with an unclear origin.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscellaneous">Miscellaneous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Miscellaneous">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2015 the National Videogame Arcade was opened in the Hockley area of the city; being "the UK's first cultural centre for videogames".<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In June 2018 it was announced that it would close in September before being relocated to Sheffield in October.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham has hosted an annual Asian Mela every summer since about 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Nottingham also hosts a parade on St Patrick's Day,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Fireworks at the Chinese New Year, Holi in the Park celebrating Hinduism,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> a West Indian-style carnival, and several Sikh events.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham has featured in a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_fiction_set_in_Nottingham" title="List of fiction set in Nottingham">fictional works</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Nottingham" title="Sport in Nottingham">Sport in Nottingham</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg/220px-Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg/330px-Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg/440px-Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham_MMB_15_City_Ground.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/City_Ground" title="City Ground">City Ground</a> by the <a href="/wiki/River_Trent" title="River Trent">River Trent</a></div></div></div>
<p>Nottingham is home to two professional football clubs: <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a>. Their two football grounds, facing each other on opposite sides of the River Trent, are noted for geographically being the closest in English league football. Notts County, formed in 1862, is the oldest professional football club in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> They were also among the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a>'s founder members in 1888. For most of their history they have played their home games at <a href="/wiki/Meadow_Lane" title="Meadow Lane">Meadow Lane</a>, which currently holds some 20,000 spectators, all seated. They currently play in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Two">Football League Two</a>, at Level 4 in the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a> (most recently played at Level 1 in May 1992).<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Nottingham Forest, who currently play in the Level 2 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a>, were English Level 1 champions in 1978 and won the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup">European Cup</a> twice over the next two seasons under the management of <a href="/wiki/Brian_Clough" title="Brian Clough">Brian Clough</a>, who was the club's manager from January 1975 to May 1993, leading them to four <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> triumphs in that time. They have played at the <a href="/wiki/City_Ground" title="City Ground">City Ground</a>, on the south bank of the <a href="/wiki/River_Trent" title="River Trent">River Trent</a>, since 1898. Nottingham Forest joined the Football League in 1892, four years after its inception when it merged with the rival <a href="/wiki/Football_Alliance" title="Football Alliance">Football Alliance</a>, and 100 years later, they were among the <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">FA Premier League</a>'s founder members in 1992—though they have not played top division football since May 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/City_Ground" title="City Ground">City Ground</a> played host to group stage games in the <a href="/wiki/Euro_96" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 96">1996 European Football Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham won the title of 2015 City of Football after five months of campaigning, which resulted in £1.6m in funding for local football ventures and to encourage more people to play the sport.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Nottingham was selected to be a host city for the <a href="/wiki/England_2018_FIFA_World_Cup_bid" title="England 2018 FIFA World Cup bid">England 2018 FIFA World Cup bid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> It was proposed that if the bid were successful, the city would have received a new Nottingham Forest Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nottinghamshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Nottinghamshire County Cricket Club">Nottinghamshire County Cricket Club</a> play at <a href="/wiki/Trent_Bridge" title="Trent Bridge">Trent Bridge</a>—an international cricket venue. The club were 2010 Cricket County Champions. Trent Bridge cricket ground is a host of <a href="/wiki/Test_Cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="Test Cricket">Test Cricket</a>, and was one of the venues for the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009 ICC World Twenty20</a>.
</p><p>The Rugby team, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_R.F.C." title="Nottingham R.F.C.">Nottingham R.F.C.</a>, have played their home games at <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a>, Notts County's <a href="/wiki/Meadow_Lane" title="Meadow Lane">Meadow Lane</a> stadium since 2006. In January 2015 they will play home matches at their training base, Lady Bay Sports Ground. Currently in the <a href="/wiki/RFU_Championship" title="RFU Championship">RFU Championship</a>, if Nottingham are promoted to the <a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" class="mw-redirect" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">Rugby Premiership</a> they will return to Meadow Lane for home matches.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Outlaws_(rugby_league_team)" title="Nottingham Outlaws (rugby league team)">Nottingham Outlaws</a> are an amateur Rugby League club who play in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Conference_National_Division" title="Rugby League Conference National Division">Rugby League Conference National Division</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Caesars" title="Nottingham Caesars">Nottingham Caesars</a> who were formed in 1984 play in the <a href="/wiki/BAFA_National_Leagues" title="BAFA National Leagues">British American Football League</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Hadden_Stadium" title="Harvey Hadden Stadium">Harvey Hadden Stadium</a>.
</p><p>The city was the birthplace and training location for <a href="/wiki/Ice_dancer" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice dancer">ice dancers</a> <a href="/wiki/Torvill_and_Dean" title="Torvill and Dean">Torvill and Dean</a>, who won Gold at the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">1984 Sarajevo Olympics</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Ice_Centre" title="National Ice Centre">National Ice Centre</a>, opened by Bob the Builder, is a national centre for ice sports. The square in-front of the centre is named "Bolero Square" after Torvill and Dean's perfect 6.0 performance. Nottingham is home to the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Panthers" title="Nottingham Panthers">Nottingham Panthers</a> ice hockey team.
</p><p>Other sporting events in the city include the annual tennis <a href="/wiki/Aegon_Trophy" title="Aegon Trophy">Aegon Trophy</a> (which is staged at the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Tennis_Centre" title="Nottingham Tennis Centre">City of Nottingham Tennis Centre</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_Marathon" class="mw-redirect" title="Robin Hood Marathon">Robin Hood Marathon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Milk Race">Milk Race</a>, the Great Nottinghamshire Bike Ride<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> and the Outlaw Triathlon.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Nottingham also has two <a href="/wiki/Roller_derby" title="Roller derby">Roller derby</a> teams: the Nottingham Roller Girls<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Hellfire_Harlots" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellfire Harlots">Hellfire Harlots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2015, Nottingham was named as the official Home of Sport by VisitEngland for its contributions and recognition of the developments of the games of Football, Cricket, Ice Hockey in Britain, Boxing, Tennis and general Athletics, Gymnastics and Water sports.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Nottingham" title="Transport in Nottingham">Transport in Nottingham</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham_railway_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nottingham_railway_station.jpg/220px-Nottingham_railway_station.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nottingham_railway_station.jpg/330px-Nottingham_railway_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nottingham_railway_station.jpg/440px-Nottingham_railway_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham_railway_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham railway station</a></div></div></div>
<p>Nottingham is served by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a> (formerly known as Nottingham East Midlands Airport until it reverted to its original name), near Castle Donington in North West Leicestershire, just under 15 miles (24&#160;km) south-west of the city centre.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham Station">Nottingham Station</a>, the second busiest railway station in the Midlands for passenger entries and exits,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> provides rail services for the city; with connections operated by <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canalside_Nottingham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canalside_Nottingham.jpg/220px-Canalside_Nottingham.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canalside_Nottingham.jpg/330px-Canalside_Nottingham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canalside_Nottingham.jpg/440px-Canalside_Nottingham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canalside_Nottingham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Waterways building (formerly the <a href="/wiki/Trent_Navigation_Company" title="Trent Navigation Company">Trent Navigation Company</a> warehouse) on the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Canal" title="Nottingham Canal">Nottingham Canal</a></div></div></div>
<p>The reintroduction of <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Express_Transit" title="Nottingham Express Transit">trams</a> in 2004 made Nottingham the newest of only six English cities to have a light rail system.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The trams run from the city centre to <a href="/wiki/Hucknall" title="Hucknall">Hucknall</a> in the north, with a spur to the Phoenix Park Park and Ride close to Junction 26 of the M1. Two new lines opened in 2015 extending the network to the southern suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Wilford" title="Wilford">Wilford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clifton,_Nottingham" title="Clifton, Nottingham">Clifton</a> and the western suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Beeston,_Nottinghamshire" title="Beeston, Nottinghamshire">Beeston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chilwell" title="Chilwell">Chilwell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has the largest public bus network in the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-Our_Companies_–_NCT_–_Transdev_UK_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our_Companies_–_NCT_–_Transdev_UK-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In September 2010, Nottingham was named "England's least car-dependent city" by the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Better_Transport_(United_Kingdom)" title="Campaign for Better Transport (United Kingdom)">Campaign for Better Transport</a> with London and Manchester in second and fourth place respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In November 2010, Nottingham City Council won Transport Authority of the Year by the UK Bus Awards, for services for providing safer and sustainable public transport.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham's waterways, now primarily used for leisure, have been extensively used for transport in the past.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span id="Crime"></span> 
Nottingham is served by <a href="/wiki/Nottinghamshire_Police" title="Nottinghamshire Police">Nottinghamshire Police</a> and has a <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Crown_Court" title="Nottingham Crown Court">Crown Court</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Magistrates%27_Court" title="Nottingham Magistrates&#39; Court">Magistrates' Court</a>.
</p><p>Laurie Macdonald of <i>Inside One</i> magazine observes that the city's former high crime rate earned it the nickname "Shottingham", but that by 2013 this image was outdated. The article was written in response to a <a href="/wiki/USwitch" title="USwitch">uSwitch</a> survey that had found south Nottinghamshire to be the fourth-best place to live in the UK in terms of living standards. Crime in Nottingham had also fallen by three-quarters since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham-cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Nottingham-cathedral.jpg/170px-Nottingham-cathedral.jpg" width="170" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Nottingham-cathedral.jpg/255px-Nottingham-cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Nottingham-cathedral.jpg/340px-Nottingham-cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nottingham-cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Cathedral" title="Nottingham Cathedral">Roman Catholic Cathedral of St. Barnabas</a> from Derby Road</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar,_Nottingham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar%2C_Nottingham.jpg/170px-Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar%2C_Nottingham.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar%2C_Nottingham.jpg/255px-Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar%2C_Nottingham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar%2C_Nottingham.jpg/340px-Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar%2C_Nottingham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2314" data-file-height="3474" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_with_Pitcher_and_Piano_cocktail_bar,_Nottingham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Unitarian Chapel on <a href="/wiki/High_Pavement" title="High Pavement">High Pavement</a>, now the <a href="/wiki/High_Pavement_Chapel" title="High Pavement Chapel">Pitcher and Piano public house</a></div></div></div>
<p>Historically, the requirement for city status was the presence of a (Church of England) cathedral. Nottingham, however, does not have one, having only been designated a city in 1897, in celebration of Queen Victoria's Diamond Jubilee. From around AD 1100 Nottingham was part of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Lichfield" title="Diocese of Lichfield">Diocese of Lichfield</a>, controlled as an <a href="/wiki/List_of_Archdeacons_of_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Archdeacons of Nottingham">archdeaconry</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lichfield_Cathedral" title="Lichfield Cathedral">Lichfield Cathedral</a> in Staffordshire. However, in 1837 the archdeaconry was placed under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Lincoln" title="Diocese of Lincoln">Diocese of Lincoln</a>. In 1884 it became part of the newly created <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Southwell_and_Nottingham" title="Diocese of Southwell and Nottingham">Diocese of Southwell</a>, which it, and the city, are still part of today. The bishop is based at <a href="/wiki/Southwell_Minster" title="Southwell Minster">Southwell Minster</a>, 14 miles (23&#160;km) north-east of the city.
</p><p>Despite not having a cathedral, Nottingham has three notable historic <a href="/wiki/Anglican_parish_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican parish church">Anglican parish churches</a>, all of which date back to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Church,_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Mary&#39;s Church, Nottingham">St. Mary the Virgin</a>, in the Lace Market, is the oldest and largest. The church dates from the eighth or ninth centuries, but the present building is at least the third on the site, dating primarily from 1377 to 1485. St. Mary's is considered the mother church of the city and civic services are held here, including the welcome to the new <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of Nottingham">Lord Mayor of Nottingham</a> each year. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Churches_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Churches Group">Greater Churches Group</a>. <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church,_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter&#39;s Church, Nottingham">St. Peter's</a> in the heart of the city is the oldest building in continuous use in Nottingham, with traces of building starting in 1180. <a href="/wiki/St._Nicholas%27_Church,_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Nicholas&#39; Church, Nottingham">St. Nicholas'</a> is the third.
</p><p>A variety of chapels and meeting rooms are in the town. Many of these grand buildings have been demolished, including <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Place_Wesleyan_Chapel" title="Halifax Place Wesleyan Chapel">Halifax Place Wesleyan Chapel</a>, but some have been re-used, notably <a href="/wiki/High_Pavement_Chapel" title="High Pavement Chapel">High Pavement Chapel</a> which is now a public house. There are three <a href="/wiki/Christadelphian" class="mw-redirect" title="Christadelphian">Christadelphian</a> meeting halls in the city and the national headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Congregational_Federation" title="Congregational Federation">Congregational Federation</a> is in Nottingham.
</p><p>Nottingham is one of 18 British cities that do not have an Anglican cathedral.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> It is, however, home to the <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Cathedral" title="Nottingham Cathedral">Roman Catholic Cathedral of St. Barnabas</a>, which was designed by <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Pugin" title="Augustus Pugin">Augustus Pugin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consecration" title="Consecration">consecrated</a> in 1844. It is the cathedral church for the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Nottingham">Diocese of Nottingham</a>.
</p><p>Today there are places of worship for all major religions, including Christianity and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> with 32 mosques in Nottingham.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nottingham has 80,000 Christians, 30,000 Muslims, 15,000 Sikhs, 8,000 Hindus and 2,000 Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Nottingham" title="Demography of Nottingham">Demography of Nottingham</a></div>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">ONS</a> 2014 basis population projections indicate that the city is once again in a phase of steady population growth and that the 350,000 mark should be reached around 2030.
</p><p>The city of Nottingham has a population at 312,900 with the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Nottingham">Greater Nottingham</a> population at 729,977 and the Metro population at 1,543,000. The city of Nottingham has a density of 4,073/km2.
</p><p>65.4% are White British, 6.1% are European/North American, 13.1% Asian, 4.3% African, 1.6% Middle Eastern, 1.1% South/Central American and 8.2% of West Indian origins. Nottingham is a very multi-cultural city with people from 93 different countries and 101 spoken languages with cuisines, religious institutions/places of worship, businesses and supermarkets all over Nottingham especially situated in <a href="/wiki/Hyson_Green" title="Hyson Green">Hyson Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest_Fields" title="Forest Fields">Forest Fields</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carrington,_Nottingham" title="Carrington, Nottingham">Carrington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radford,_Nottingham" title="Radford, Nottingham">Radford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenton,_Nottingham" title="Lenton, Nottingham">Lenton</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Meadows,_Nottingham" title="The Meadows, Nottingham">Meadows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk,_Nottingham" title="Dunkirk, Nottingham">Dunkirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rylands" title="Rylands">Rylands</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Ann%27s,_Nottingham" title="St Ann&#39;s, Nottingham">St Ann's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sneinton" title="Sneinton">Sneinton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aspley,_Nottingham" title="Aspley, Nottingham">Aspley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broxtowe" title="Broxtowe">Broxtowe</a>, City, <a href="/wiki/Basford,_Nottinghamshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Basford, Nottinghamshire">Basford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield,_Nottingham" title="Bakersfield, Nottingham">Bakersfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlton,_Nottinghamshire" title="Carlton, Nottinghamshire">Carlton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arnold,_Nottinghamshire" title="Arnold, Nottinghamshire">Arnold</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television"><a href="/wiki/LeftLion" title="LeftLion">Television</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/BBC_East_Midlands" title="BBC East Midlands">BBC East Midlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Studios,_Nottingham" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlton Studios, Nottingham">Carlton Studios, Nottingham</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has its <a href="/wiki/BBC_East_Midlands" title="BBC East Midlands">East Midlands</a> headquarters in Nottingham on London Road. <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_East_Midlands_Today" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC East Midlands Today">BBC East Midlands Today</a></i> is broadcast from the city every weeknight at 6.30&#160;pm.
</p><p>From 1983 to 2005 <a href="/wiki/ITV_Central" title="ITV Central">Central Television</a> (the <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> region for the east Midlands) had a studio complex on Lenton Lane, producing programmes for various networks and broadcasting regional news.
</p><p>The city was recently granted permission by Ofcom to set up its own local television station. After a tender process, Confetti College was awarded the licence. The station was declared open by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Harry" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Harry">Prince Harry</a> in April 2013 and <i>Notts TV</i> began broadcast in spring 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to the national commercial and BBC radio stations, the Nottingham area is served by licensed commercial radio stations (though all broadcast to a wider area than the city).
</p><p>Radio stations include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Nottingham" title="BBC Radio Nottingham">BBC Radio Nottingham</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gold_(radio)" title="Gold (radio)">Gold</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gem_106" title="Gem 106">Gem 106</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capital_East_Midlands" title="Capital East Midlands">Capital East Midlands</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smooth_Radio_East_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Smooth Radio East Midlands">Smooth Radio East Midlands</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kemet_FM" title="Kemet FM">Kemet FM</a></li>
<li>Radio Dawn</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_radio">Student radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Student radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city's two universities both broadcast their own student radio stations. Nottingham Trent University's <a href="/w/index.php?title=FlyFM&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="FlyFM (page does not exist)">FlyFM</a> is based at the university's city campus and is broadcast online.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Nottingham University's <a href="/wiki/University_Radio_Nottingham" title="University Radio Nottingham">University Radio Nottingham</a> is broadcast around the main and Sutton Bonnington campuses on medium wave (AM), as well as over the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers_and_magazines">Newspapers and magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Newspapers and magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nottingham's main local newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Post" title="Nottingham Post">Nottingham Post</a></i>, is owned by <a href="/wiki/Northcliffe_Media" title="Northcliffe Media">Northcliffe Media</a> and is published daily from Monday to Saturday each week.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/LeftLion" title="LeftLion">LeftLion magazine</a> (established 2003) is distributed for free across the city. Covering Nottingham culture including music, art, theatre, comedy, food and drink.
</p><p>Student tabloid <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tab" title="The Tab">The Tab</a></i> also publishes online content and has teams at both universities.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg/220px-Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg/330px-Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg/440px-Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wollaton_Hall" title="Wollaton Hall">Wollaton Hall</a> was used as <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Manor" title="Wayne Manor">Wayne Manor</a> in the Batman film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Nottingham has been used as a location in many locally, nationally, and internationally produced films. Movies that have been filmed (partly or entirely) in Nottingham include:<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_cities">Twin cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Twin cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in the United Kingdom">List of twin towns and sister cities in the United Kingdom</a></div>
